<div id="review_793828217" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793828217" />
    <a title="Shalon Lippert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250685-shalon-lippert"><img alt="Shalon Lippert" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/793828217?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shalon Lippert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shalon Lippert" href="/user/show/2250685-shalon-lippert">Shalon Lippert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer793828217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16748267119522897338">This book is deliciously awful. I hated every moment of the purple prose and outrageously absurd dialogue. The "love" scenes were disgusting and completely unsatisfying. Cathy's story reads like some twisted Mary Sue.<br/><br/>And yet. I could not put it down. In the back of my mind, as I read on, I wanted to shake my fist at God for placing such a damnable book on earth! Oh! How I hated Cathy, who harbored spite in her soul like some packrat hiding strings and bits of plastic trash and scraps of bread an</span>
  <span id="freeText16748267119522897338" style="display:none">This book is deliciously awful. I hated every moment of the purple prose and outrageously absurd dialogue. The "love" scenes were disgusting and completely unsatisfying. Cathy's story reads like some twisted Mary Sue.<br /><br />And yet. I could not put it down. In the back of my mind, as I read on, I wanted to shake my fist at God for placing such a damnable book on earth! Oh! How I hated Cathy, who harbored spite in her soul like some packrat hiding strings and bits of plastic trash and scraps of bread and greasy meat in her uber nest inside a dark, moist crawlspace. And yet I loved her, yes, that I can admit to myself. In the deepest recesses of my mind I can admit that the sincerest hope of my innermost soul was to see Cathy learn to find and accept love, to cast aside the entanglements of self-interested men. To confront the horror of her life and choose the path in the sun! I hungrily consumed page after page of the wretched, incestuous plot that she wove to exact revenge upon her cruel mother and grandmother. As the story went on, in my mind's eye I held Cathy before me and plead with her: Please! Stop this at once! Don't you see? Don't you understand what your anger has turned you into? You made a daily meal of spite and anger and now it has utterly consumed you. Poor Carrie, poor little Carrie only wanted to be loved -but you nursed your hatred for Corrine rather than your love for your sister who was also your daughter. Didn't you, you, naive and presumptuous woman-child!<br />No! I resolved never to read If There Be Thorns! Never! As I turned page 374 and wondered when I could finally stop this never ending spiral of tragedy and despair, I forced myself on. Yet I didn't have to force myself. The book forced itself on me. It insisted on telling me its story. It pressed it's body into the curve of my yielding frame. I felt its rigid hardness against the supple curve of my hip as I begged the brute to let me alone! But it insisted and suddenly it was on top of me, pressing to my lips, stealing my breath, calling me a tease for wanting to turn away after I had so brazenly and haughtily made my challenge known. <br />And just as I began to breathe a sigh of relief that this wriggling, hairy demon on top of me would finally give out, exhausted from its toils, I read the last two pages. Damn you, God! Damn, damn, damn you... I knew then that this monster had not finished with me. It would return to me again and again, having its way with me until the Dollanganger story was all told and the demon was satiated. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16748267119522897338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_22984687" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22984687" />
    <a title="Trudy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1036503-trudy"><img alt="Trudy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470821147p2/1036503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22984687?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trudy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trudy" href="/user/show/1036503-trudy">Trudy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22984687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6191484064461623445">My books are tattered and dog eared... I couldn't put these books down when I was in high school. Read the whole series twice. Which says alot at a time in most teenagers lives when they are repulsed by reading anything that isn't required by school.<br/><br/>So, just when you think the kids are going to be all right - after escaping Grandmama's evil clutches - they go and find bigger and better ways to mess up their lives... and I root for the remaining Dollangagner kids all the way.<br/><br/>Chris is unshakable i</span>
  <span id="freeText6191484064461623445" style="display:none">My books are tattered and dog eared... I couldn't put these books down when I was in high school. Read the whole series twice. Which says alot at a time in most teenagers lives when they are repulsed by reading anything that isn't required by school.<br /><br />So, just when you think the kids are going to be all right - after escaping Grandmama's evil clutches - they go and find bigger and better ways to mess up their lives... and I root for the remaining Dollangagner kids all the way.<br /><br />Chris is unshakable in his love (and not the normal brotherly kind) for his sister, Cathy. Cathy is, however, unshakable in her need for revenge on her mother and grandmother. They are growing up, and while Chris and Carrie go away to school. Cathy stays at home with Dr. Paul (the man who ends up taking them in and saving them). No good is to come of any of this... A train wreck for sure, but you know human nature - we can't not watch it...<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6191484064461623445" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_364418172" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/364418172" />
    <a title="Stephanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7683989-stephanie"><img alt="Stephanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367867289p2/7683989.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/364418172?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie" href="/user/show/7683989-stephanie">Stephanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer364418172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16669106825167154772">I am crazy psyched because I had no idea that there were 3 more of these wacko books, so I am going to go find the next one asap.<br/><br/>As a sequel, this was nearly as perverted and warped as the first. First we have the kind doctor who takes in the three POWs. Chris has a mentor now, Cathy can do her ballet, and Carrie can start growing her body to match the size of her head. Oh but what's that, Cathy? You have the hots for the doctor! Of course you do. And where is his sense of morality and the fact </span>
  <span id="freeText16669106825167154772" style="display:none">I am crazy psyched because I had no idea that there were 3 more of these wacko books, so I am going to go find the next one asap.<br /><br />As a sequel, this was nearly as perverted and warped as the first. First we have the kind doctor who takes in the three POWs. Chris has a mentor now, Cathy can do her ballet, and Carrie can start growing her body to match the size of her head. Oh but what's that, Cathy? You have the hots for the doctor! Of course you do. And where is his sense of morality and the fact that she's like 16? On the floor next to her nightgown.<br /><br />Then there's Julian, the hot ballerino who also happens to be a cruel bastard who likes to kick the tar out of Cathy whenever possible. Oh she's torn between the handsome elder doctor and the young hot domestic abuser. Oh well, let's marry the hitter. In between all this mess, Chris is super jealous bc he wants to marry his sister (ew) and Carrie gets sent to boarding school. Because that is exactly what she needed, to be separated from all the people she trusts to get tormented by young girls.<br /><br />My favorite is Cathy's sweet revenge on her mother, especially when she decides to go after her man. (This is, of course, after the demise of Julian and more waiting around by the good Doctor). This tale truly twists and turns. Cathy gets her revenge, but at what price?<br /><br />What happened to Carrie? Oh, well, no one was paying attention to her anyways.<br /><br />4 stars for pure chaos. You have to admit, it's entertainment at it's finest.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BybdvIaEsoI4AFBW0JshysrF3RmdUxWlETq4V1R9ZZM83pedUZfNgDtEc06V+68q47PQpLERUJgVDsNUDo2sbg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LbkRNglcVukuS359ynggROEz3V3Qjz2jv2PKUDEObRkWQVsX3k8p6y0PXWWPGK6kyEXQ4PzNeJ67V7FTa/6k5A==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1353301.V_C_Andrews">About V.C. Andrews</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1353301.V_C_Andrews"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1413410493p3/1353301.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/1353301.V_C_Andrews">V.C. Andrews
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
6,092
followers
</div>

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1367386078269675649"><b>Books published under the following names - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13312974._Virginia_Andrews' title=' Virginia Andrews' rel='nofollow noopener'> Virginia Andrews</a>, V. Andrews, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14980120._Virginia_C__Andrews' title=' Virginia C. Andrews' rel='nofollow noopener'> Virginia C. Andrews</a> & V.C. Endrius. Books since her death ghost written by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/145370.Andrew_Neiderman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Andrew Neiderman</a>, but still attributed to the V.C. Andrews name</b><br/><br/>Virginia Cleo Andrews (born Cleo Virginia Andrews) was born June 6, 1923 in Portsmouth, Virginia. The youngest child and the only daughter of William Henry Andrews, a career navy man who</span>
  <span id="freeText1367386078269675649" style="display:none"><b>Books published under the following names - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13312974._Virginia_Andrews" title=" Virginia Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener"> Virginia Andrews</a>, V. Andrews, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14980120._Virginia_C__Andrews" title=" Virginia C. Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener"> Virginia C. Andrews</a> &amp; V.C. Endrius. Books since her death ghost written by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/145370.Andrew_Neiderman" rel="nofollow noopener">Andrew Neiderman</a>, but still attributed to the V.C. Andrews name</b><br /><br />Virginia Cleo Andrews (born Cleo Virginia Andrews) was born June 6, 1923 in Portsmouth, Virginia. The youngest child and the only daughter of William Henry Andrews, a career navy man who opened a tool-and-die business after retirement, and Lillian Lilnora Parker Andrews, a telephone operator. She spent her happy childhood years in Portsmouth, Virginia, living briefly in Rochester, New York. The Andrews family returned to Portsmouth while Virginia was in high school.<br /><br />While a teenager, Virginia suffered a tragic accident, falling down the stairs at her school and incurred severe back injuries. Arthritis and a failed spinal surgical procedure forced her to spend most of her life on crutches or in a wheelchair.<br /><br />Virginia excelled in school and, at fifteen, won a scholarship for writing a parody of Tennyson's <i>Idylls of the King</i>. She proudly earned her diploma from Woodrow Wilson High School in Portsmouth. After graduation, she nurtured her artistic talent by completing a four-year correspondence art course while living at home with her family.<br /><br />After William Andrews died in the late 1960s, Virginia helped to support herself and her mother through her extremely successful career as a commercial artist, portrait painter, and fashion illustrator.<br /><br />Frustrated with the lack of creative satisfaction that her work provided, Virginia sought creative release through writing, which she did in secret. In 1972, she completed her first novel, <i>The Gods of the Green Mountain</i> [sic], a science-fantasy story. It was never published. Between 1972 and 1979, she wrote nine novels and twenty short stories, of which only one was published. "I Slept with My Uncle on My Wedding Night", a short fiction piece, was published in a pulp confession magazine.<br /><br />Promise gleamed over the horizon for Virginia when she submitted a 290,000-word novel, <i>The Obsessed</i>, to a publishing company. She was told that the story had potential, but needed to be trimmed and spiced up a bit. She drafted a new outline in a single night and added "unspeakable things my mother didn't want me to write about." The ninety-eight-page revision was re-titled <i>Flowers in the Attic</i> and she was paid a $7,500 advance. Her new-generation Gothic novel reached the bestseller lists a mere two weeks after its 1979 paperback publication by Pocket Books.<br /><br /><i>Petals on the Wind</i>, her sequel to <i>Flowers</i>, was published the next year, earning Virginia a $35,000 advance. The second book remained on the New York Times bestseller list for an unbelievable nineteen weeks (<i>Flowers</i> also returned to the list). These first two novels alone sold over seven million copies in only two years. The third novel of the Dollanganger series, <i>If There Be Thorns</i>, was released in 1981, bringing Virginia a $75,000 advance. It reached No. 2 on many bestseller lists within its first two weeks.<br /><br />Taking a break from the chronicles of Chris and Cathy Dollanganger, Virginia published her one, and only, stand-alone novel, <i>My Sweet Audrina</i>, in 1982. The book welcomed an immediate success, topping the sales figures of her previous novels. Two years later, a fourth Dollanganger novel was released, <i>Seeds of Yesterday</i>. According to the New York Times, <i>Seeds</i> was the best-selling fiction paperback novel of 1984. Also in 1984, V.C. Andrews was named "Professional Woman of the Year" by the city of Norfolk, Virginia.<br /><br />Upon Andrews's death in 1986, two final novels—<i>Garden of Shadows</i> and <i>Fallen Hearts</i>—were published. These two novels are considered the last to bear the "V.C. Andrews" name and to be almost completely written by </span>
  <a data-text-id="1367386078269675649" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
